<div id="review_212801108" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/212801108" />
    <a title="Suzanne " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5952567-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411233665p2/5952567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/212801108?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne " href="/user/show/5952567-suzanne">Suzanne </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781907411038" href="/book/show/11438966-until-i-die">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5952567-suzanne?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5952567-suzanne?shelf=immortals">immortals</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer212801108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2482276177658824247">I'm so mad right now. I really didn't enjoy this book, at all. But I struggled through it because I really enjoyed Die for Me and hoped that the third book will be better. I only started to enjoy this at the very end, and then it ends on a massive cliffhanger. grrr<br/><br/>Review: <br/>Well, it took me five days to get through this book and I think that speaks volumes. I really struggled with Until I Die, a book I had been really looking forward to reading, having absolutely loving Die for Me. <br/><br/>It's been a whi</span>
  <span id="freeText2482276177658824247" style="display:none">I'm so mad right now. I really didn't enjoy this book, at all. But I struggled through it because I really enjoyed Die for Me and hoped that the third book will be better. I only started to enjoy this at the very end, and then it ends on a massive cliffhanger. grrr<br /><br />Review: <br />Well, it took me five days to get through this book and I think that speaks volumes. I really struggled with Until I Die, a book I had been really looking forward to reading, having absolutely loving Die for Me. <br /><br />It's been a while since I read Die for Me so I don't remember every little detail, just the enjoyment I had from reading it. So I was very surprised to find myself feeling quite negative towards Kate. She just really didn't appeal to me throughout this book. <br /><br />But I was still completely in adoration of Vincent, and that's probably what kept me going. The hardship that he was going through in this book for Kate just pee'd me off. While we don't find out exactly what it is until the end, we do know that it's not something that's doing him any good. He has bags under his eyes and sometimes literally looks like death warmed up. While I admired him for doing it, and trying to make it easier on Kate being with him, I felt that he shouldn't have to be doing anything, that she should have just accepted him as he was. <br /><br />I very quickly guessed who the enemy was going to be and didnt' like them from the start. A lot of the time I had an idea what was going on with their motives and couldn't figure out how no one else could see it, so needless to say, that was very annoying.<br /><br />The secondary characters that we know and love from Die for Me actually play very little part in Until I Die and I missed the banter I had enjoyed between them all previously.<br /><br />Kate begins to do her own sleuthing then on trying to find a cure for Vincent which does add a little bit more interest, but this isn't until almost halfway through. We learn more about the history of the Revenant's and the Numa and of a prophecy that tells of a Champion among the Revenant's, who will be able to destroy the Numa once and for all. But the person who kills the Champion, will automatically take all their powers.<br /><br />Any action or excitement in this book didn't occur until the very end. And then it ends on a woeful cliffhanger. I was left feeling so mad that I just wanted to fling this book out of the nearest window. I couldn't believe that I had struggled through this boring, dullness for the past five days for it to end with that. <br /><br />Obviously, such a cliffhanger ensures that I will indeed pick up the next book despite the fact that this was pure insipidness. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2482276177658824247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4016030-isamlq?shelf=arc-galley">arc-galley</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer301447536" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9437197897558716711">This didn’t work for me and that’s even with more of the revenant/ numa aspect explained. Too much of it revolved around Kate and Vincent together and them figuring out a way to make their time together longer/easier/more bearable for one or both of them. If the first book had me remarking on how absolutely ordinary she came across, that is sometimes pissed off but normally thinking and wary… here Kate’s less of what she was back then. Here, she’s all 'coquettish' and flirty with Vincent. And I </span>
  <span id="freeText9437197897558716711" style="display:none">This didn’t work for me and that’s even with more of the revenant/ numa aspect explained. Too much of it revolved around Kate and Vincent together and them figuring out a way to make their time together longer/easier/more bearable for one or both of them. If the first book had me remarking on how absolutely ordinary she came across, that is sometimes pissed off but normally thinking and wary… here Kate’s less of what she was back then. Here, she’s all 'coquettish' and flirty with Vincent. And I get that they're not out of their “honeymoon period” yet, but it did get a bit much. <br /><br />So yeah, you could say that the romance had been kicked up a notch (several notches, I suppose). Though I could have lived with it being all about them if there were something more to look forward to. As is though, UNTIL YOU DIE focused on them and rarely went beyond the two. And when it did touch on something not involving the couple (rarely, by the way) things felt short to me. <br /><br />Anyway beyond the two were a couple of new players who were so obviously not who they said they were, a couple of <s>interesting</s> <s> annoying</s> moments of selfishness by both the main protags... And, I concede, some interesting moments with a couple of the supporting characters. Jules in particular had me wondering about his role in books to come especially with the way things ended in this one. <br /><br />Speak of the ending: it might well be the only thing in this sequel that could get me to read what happens next. To say that it’s atypical and not the expected HEA is an absolute truth. <br /><br /><b>THANKS Edelweiss!<br />2/5</b><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8327085869955551704">*Reread Jan 2020<br/><br/>It has been years since I’ve read this series. And I truly see how I’ve grown as a reader. <br/><br/>This wasn’t a bad book. Actually I loved it before, but I see the flaws in this series clear as day making me think it’s an ok read overall.<br/><br/>The suspense kills me at times, while the plot is inherently predictable too.   <span id="freeText8327085869955551704" style="display:none">*Reread Jan 2020<br /><br />It has been years since I’ve read this series. And I truly see how I’ve grown as a reader. <br /><br />This wasn’t a bad book. Actually I loved it before, but I see the flaws in this series clear as day making me think it’s an ok read overall.<br /><br />The suspense kills me at times, while the plot is inherently predictable too. That in and of itself is indeed One of the biggest flaws of this book. The intensity in the plot came near the end. Why it took an entire book to get to a climax of a book is crazy to me but I guess it is what it is.<br /><br />The characters were the characters. Now, I did see growth in the characters and that says growth in the writing. The characters are developing nicely, but are still predictable in my opinion but then again this book is an older book so I’m not gonna be too picky about that at this point.<br /><br />One of the things that I thought the author could have added to put so much more power into the characters is adding little stuff that features their period they are from. In a way, this is a period piece so why not play off of it? The author tried, but didn’t quite succeed at that fully.<br /><br />Overall I enjoyed the book. That’s why it’s at a 4.0 star rating!<br /><br />*Reread Jan 2020*<br /><br />I read this a few years ago so I do not really remember much of my pinons about this book, but since I reviewed the first book I know I like that one. So I'm assuming I like this one as well!</span>

<div id="review_257893574" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/257893574" />
    <a title="Teresa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5754823-teresa"><img alt="Teresa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345839967p2/5754823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/257893574?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teresa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teresa" href="/user/show/5754823-teresa">Teresa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People that liked Die For Me and could forgive minor flaws easily</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Teresa by: </span>
      Me, myself, and I 
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257893574" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6975406143679227538">I like Until I Die every bit as much I liked Die For Me, though a little less this time. For me, I feel like Until I Die is a middle book, and although it didn't quite disappoint me much like other sequels love to do to me these days, I feel like Amy Plum abandoned all of the magic and enchantment of DFM that made it memorable. I will say, though, that Until I Die has redeeming qualities and, in lots of ways, is better than DFM. I love the world of Amy Plum, complete with a fun and new kind of s</span>
  <span id="freeText6975406143679227538" style="display:none">I like Until I Die every bit as much I liked Die For Me, though a little less this time. For me, I feel like Until I Die is a middle book, and although it didn't quite disappoint me much like other sequels love to do to me these days, I feel like Amy Plum abandoned all of the magic and enchantment of DFM that made it memorable. I will say, though, that Until I Die has redeeming qualities and, in lots of ways, is better than DFM. I love the world of Amy Plum, complete with a fun and new kind of supernatural creature- the revenants- (thumbs up for originality), a well descripted Parisian setting, a shy protagonist with a quiet determination, a swoon worthy love interest, very likeable secondary characters, and a war between two sides that's ready to change each one of the characters' lives. What's not to like?<br /><br />It took me quite a bit of a longer time to get into this book than it did for me to get into DFM. For about 100 pages, I felt as if the pages dragged on and on, but when it got to the part where Kate was looking for the miracle cure to help resist Vincent's temptation to die, that was when I began sitting up. I like to say at this point that this part is original. I was thinking, at the ending of DFM and the beginning of UID, that Plum would have to make a Breaking Dawn move and change Kate into a revenant to be with Vincent. I'm happy that may no longer have to be the case anymore. I think that authors that write paranormal-human romances need to be more creative as to how to get the immortal, ageless boy and the mortal girl together, and not take the easy way out, copy Stephanie Meyers, and transform the girl into the supernatural creature. So Until I Die is a refreshing exception to that. <br /><br />Of course, my favorite thing about this series will always be Jules, Georgia, and Charlotte. Unfortunately, Jules and Charlotte didn't make as much appearances as I would have liked, but Georgia made a big impact in UID. I love Kate's unconditional, sweet relationship with her sister and the way that Georgia will always have Kate's back and everything. I also really like Charlotte, especially in the first book, and although she didn't have a large role in this installment, I still find her character and background likeable and refreshing. And of course, Jules will always be considered my favorite character ever in the series. I love his snarky quips and flirty jokes. Even though I am against love triangles, I found myself wishing that Kate could have developed feelings for Jules. Nothing against Vincent, but I love Jules a lot more. And for me, in this book, Jules showed romantic interest for Kate. Maybe it could be the start of something....? <br /><br />I like Kate's romance with Vincent a lot, but in UID, I feel like their relationship lost the sparks and magic it had in DFM. Sure, they would go on dates and see each other everyday, but apparently I just didn't feel sparks. Although I find both Kate and Vincent likeable and can see what they see in one another, their romance wasn't as awesome as it was in the first book. And the fact that they kept things from each other doesn't make it easier for me to like their romance. For a good bit of the book, I was annoyed that Vincent kept refusing to answer Kate's questions on the "experiment" he was doing. I mean, that experiment would affect Kate every bit as it would affect him, and yet, he still evade her questions. And the fact that Kate went behind his back to do some sleuthing bothered me, as well. But in all honesty, I still find the love they have for each other sweet and convincing, though no longer as amazing and epic as it used to be.<br /><br />All in all, I think this book deserves every single one of my four star rating. This series is really awesome, but in some ways, I keep thinking that UID is like a middle book. I am still looking very forward to reading If I Should Die. I am a sucker for awesome cliff hangers, and I desperate want to know what Plum would do in the end to get Kate and Vincent together. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6975406143679227538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

(Pretty much spent the rest of the time playing Candy Crush.)<br/><br/>But no seriously, I’m trying to decide how I can organize my thoughts well enough to review this book in a way better than “what the fuck was that.”<br/><br/>It’s not like it was BAD. Or didn’t make sense. Or wasn’t </span></span>
  <span id="freeText17834980215746560555" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1438596613p8/1217599.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://just0nemorepage.tumblr.com/post/152477180807/until-i-die-amy-plum-revenants-2-353" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>This review is also posted on my blog.</b>
</a><br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I’m seriously just so glad that I finished with that book and can move on to another one that it made no difference that I finished at work, three hours before my shift ended. (Pretty much spent the rest of the time playing Candy Crush.)<br><br>But no seriously, I’m trying to decide how I can organize my thoughts well enough to review this book in a way better than “what the fuck was that.”<br><br>It’s not like it was BAD. Or didn’t make sense. Or wasn’t cohesive. If that was the case, I probably would’ve just gone “lol fuck this shit” and abandoned it for the book next in line. But if you read through my progress notes you’ll see what I’m talking about.<br><br>First I was like, what the hell is up with this dialogue. NO ONE talks like this. It was stilted and awkward and over-detailed and left me cringing and literally face palming and going “uggghhh” more than once. Then I was like, you’re seventeen, your relationship is five months old, holy shit, why are you pledging your life’s love to this guy. And THEN, her grandfather just *happened* to have an ancient book on revenants that he just bought for his gallery (conveniently not yet on display), and her grandmother just *happened* to know some old obscure French traditions to lead her to the healer (“leave it to Grammie to know this” my ASS), and the revenants’ household just *happened* to have the only other copy of the ancient revenants book in existence to complete the puzzle (SO CONVENIENT), and I was like FUCK ME RUNNING, I can’t handle this. AND THEN. There’s shit like “if you want the one revenant who prides herself on knowing all of revenant history to forget about the bit of juicy history you just mentioned, then WHY DID YOU MENTION IT,” and “goddamnit Jules Kate didn’t ASK you to come along as an escort for her private errand why are you yelling at her for dragging you along,” and the RANDOM DETAILS about French things being French and all the extravagance that they can (conveniently) afford and how it was so infuriating that lack of communication between Kate and Vincent was like the primary source of conflict in the whole book (god I couldn’t buy their relationship AT ALL I could almost feel my brain cells dying every time she lost all her senses in the swamp of choked up emotion she felt any time he ever did practically anything nice for her). And then I was like FUCK NOW THERE’S A CHOSEN ONE™. Oh my god seriously. A fucking prophecy. Or whatever. And Vincent is the Champion. Of COURSE he’s the fucking Champion I don’t know what I was expecting.<br><br>But then the ending surprised me enough to keep me going and actually want to read the last book in the series. idk why I subject myself to this but goddamnit now I’m curious.<br><br>Like. GASP. She might have to live without Vincent if he’s destroyed permanently? ?? ????<br><br>How incomprehensible.<br><br>And Violette turning out to be the traitor for the last 35 years under everyone’s noses highly intrigued me. But then, holy monologueing Batman. Please feel free to explain all your dastardly plans. I’ve got all day. No, please continue.<br><br>God this is such a predictable mess. But, there’s only one book left and I was like “well shit” at the end and feel like yeaaah I should give finishing the series a go.<br><br>Maybe I would’ve liked this better if I hadn’t waited two years since reading the first book? I don’t know. And I don’t really care either, I remember not finding the first book to be that spectacular either.<br><br>But again, it was interesting enough to keep me going. Hence. Why I find myself here in the first place.<br><br>I suppose, if tropey paranormal romances are your thing, you would highly enjoy something like this series. And who am I to judge anything about that, really? If you love it, then more power to you!<br><br>I just, couldn’t.<br><br>Ah, well.<br><br>On to my next book!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_168089008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/168089008" />
    <a title="Brooke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4140635-brooke"><img alt="Brooke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476044114p2/4140635.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/168089008?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brooke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brooke" href="/user/show/4140635-brooke">Brooke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer168089008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9602094995224028530">To be honest, I struggled a little getting through this one. There was a lot more information on Revenants in this installment and at times it felt a little info-dumpy (is that a real term?). Until I Die was much slower paced than Die for me, but with new characters, old nemeses, and relationship roadblocks, it was a good addition to the series nonetheless!<br/><br/>Kate and Vincent are a bit at odds in this book. They’re both trying to find a way to have a normal relationship where Vincent doesn’t need t</span>
  <span id="freeText9602094995224028530" style="display:none">To be honest, I struggled a little getting through this one. There was a lot more information on Revenants in this installment and at times it felt a little info-dumpy (is that a real term?). Until I Die was much slower paced than Die for me, but with new characters, old nemeses, and relationship roadblocks, it was a good addition to the series nonetheless!<br /><br />Kate and Vincent are a bit at odds in this book. They’re both trying to find a way to have a normal relationship where Vincent doesn’t need to sacrifice himself so often...or...um, ever. That’s all beautiful and great but then they start keeping things from each other and that is a BIG no-no in any and ALL relationships. Vamp-human relationships, mermaid-human relationships, human-human relationships annnnnd Revenant-human relationships. I really didn’t understand why they went behind each other’s backs when they’re supposed to be totally and completely in love. It really irked me. <br /><br />With that being said there were also a lot of things I loved about this book! Amy Plum delivers again when it comes to her descriptions of the Parisian setting. Some scenes I would reread because they were simply that gorgeous! Her fight scenes were also totally kick-butt! I LOVED THEM but wish there would have been some! You're holding out on us, Plum! <br /><br />I also LOVED Georgia in this sequel! I don’t know if she’s necessarily in this one more than the first, but her presence shines through tenfold! There are a ton of cute snarky sister moments and I loved that she was in on the Revenant loop! Oh! And her plus newbie Arthur equal win! &lt;3<br /><br />Then we have my Jules! *sighs* Can he please get his own spin-off? I love this boy SO MUCH. His flirty-protective-sexy self caused me to swoon hardcore. He kinda makes me wish that this series revolved not only around Revenants but a love triangle as well! And I am not a fan of those buuuuuuut I’m still holding out for Jules/Kate make out sesh! :P<br /><br />With plenty of twists, not nearly enough kisses and a SHOCKING (and I mean devastatingly shocking) ending, Until I Die is a slow-paced but captivating sequel! I can’t wait to find out what happens in If I Should Die, the final book in the Revenants trilogy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9602094995224028530" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('C6CO0VbVbsEeHOMPa67Gwhv8Jbc6TZwT4fd54HF174txwf3UuexWRtGEVq7KntnRTSfZKSHqV7gn79pn3ww8Ng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YrIjsaKp9ZnVJ7h98DAaSA0nck6yB9GSUexZaeZMzhUY01C0TZDNHhq/DdxRAAVbW/yO0KmgGjmX9PruSDUdqA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2106045308245325751">Amy Plum is the international bestselling author of the DIE FOR ME series (Indie Next List pick, Romance Times top pick, and recipient of a starred review from School Library Journal). The books have been translated into thirteen foreign languages. The trilogy is accompanied by two eNovellas entitled DIE FOR HER and DIE ONCE MORE and a compendium entitled INSIDE THE WORLD OF DIE FOR ME. <br/><br/>In DREAMFA</span>
  <span id="freeText2106045308245325751" style="display:none">Amy Plum is the international bestselling author of the DIE FOR ME series (Indie Next List pick, Romance Times top pick, and recipient of a starred review from School Library Journal). The books have been translated into thirteen foreign languages. The trilogy is accompanied by two eNovellas entitled DIE FOR HER and DIE ONCE MORE and a compendium entitled INSIDE THE WORLD OF DIE FOR ME. <br /><br />In DREAMFALL and NEVERWAKE a radical experiment to cure chronic insomnia goes wrong, and its seven teenage test subjects are plunged into a shared coma populated by one another’s nightmares; those who die in the dream will also die in real life.<br /><br />Amy's action/adventure/magic duology, AFTER THE END and UNTIL THE BEGINNING, received starred reviews from Publishers Weekly, 4 1/2 stars from RT Book Reviews, and enthusiastic reviews from Kirkus, USA Today, ALA Booklist and School Library Journal.<br /><br />After being raised in Birmingham, Alabama, in a rather restrictive environment, AMY PLUM escaped to Chicago to an even more restrictive environment at a university that expelled people for dancing. (And where she was called to the dean’s office for “wearing too much black”.) After all of that restrictiveness, she was forced to run far far away, specifically to Paris, France, where she only wore black and danced all she wanted.<br /><br />After five years in Paris, she ventured to London, where she got an M.A. in Medieval Art History, specializing in Early Sienese Painting (1260-1348) mainly because it promised almost no hope of finding a paying job afterward.<br /><br />Amy managed to find work in the world of art and antiques in New York. But after almost a decade of high-pressure lifestyle in the Big Apple, she swapped her American city for a French village of 1300 inhabitants.<br /><br />After signing with HarperCollins for the DIE FOR ME series, Amy left her job as an English professor at Tours University to write full-time. She now lives in Paris with her two kids and her black lab, Oberon.<br /><br />She is a huge fan of Edward Gorey and Maira Kalman (and collects both of their books/art), as well as David Sedaris, Amadeo Modigliani, and Ira Glass.<br /><br />Check out videos and extras from Amy at <a href="http://www.youtube.com/user/revenantcentral" rel="nofollow noopener">Revenant Central</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2106045308245325751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
